Volume of Egyptian Cotton Ginned 189

Alexandria telegram on the 14th: As of the end of June, the volume of ginned fine-staple cotton was 1,929,672 kantars, and the volume of ginned miscellaneous cotton was 5,971,166 kantars.

Food: Rice Market in River Towns is Tight in the South and Soft in the North

Xin Zha 190

Yesterday, various firms continued to receive shipments of Wuxi, Changzhou, Kunshan, thick japonica rice No. 12 and 13. There were also a dozen or so boats from Jiangyin and Yixing. The amount of Changshu northern japonica rice was also substantial. Transactions were limited. Although customer firms were active, the volume was not large. Prices for fresh goods remained unchanged. Prices for mid-grade goods were slightly lower due to thinner inventory. Thin rice varieties such as Shipu, Qingjiao, and Xitang had excellent transaction volume, reaching 2,000 to 3,000 dan. The river accumulation is nearly exhausted. Lupu pointed rice also shows signs of rising prices. There was little change in foreign pointed glutinous rice and glutinous rice. Tinglin and Zhangyan early rice are weak, showing signs of decline.

Southern Market 191

Yesterday, the source of goods for various firms was scarce. There was a slight amount of Puji old stock. Although the market situation in urban and rural stores improved due to the clear weather, deliveries were not timely. Therefore, the appetite for fresh goods remained high. Thick japonica rice prices rose sharply by one to two jiao, and the mid-range prices followed closely. Judging from the arrival and sales situation, the market was tight for high-grade goods and firm for second-grade goods. The inventory of thin rice was depleted, and the demand from Ningbo and local streets was also lacking, so prices further increased. Luyang pointed rice was considered not bad. The market situation was far from japonica rice prices, so the price increase was more significant. The arrival and sales of the Yin-hua variety were balanced with no significant gains or losses.

Flour Market Initially Weak, Then Firm 192

Yesterday, the flour market was weak in the morning opening, with mixed price fluctuations in imported wheat. However, the overall fluctuation was less than a jiao. Due to poor sales, northern firms had some re-selling. Factories slightly increased purchases recently to prepare for direct shipments to various ports. Around 100,000 was sold in long-term contracts, so the market stabilized. In the afternoon, due to renewed rainfall, the sentiment of inland firms worsened. Local speculators took the opportunity to buy, causing near-term and long-term prices to rise again. Although actual sales are sluggish, inland firms are ultimately defending the bottom price, so they must remain persistent. As a result, this month was 0.075 better than the previous day, August and September were 0.05 better, October was 0.1 better, November was 0.075 better, and December was 0.125 better.

Wheat Prices Unlikely to Rise Significantly 193

Spot Goods Sales Slow

Yesterday, the wheat futures market showed signs of initially being flat and then firm. The prices of imported wheat were small, with Chicago up two to three cents, and Canada up 0.1. Some were cautious and watched the market. Because the gold market rose again, most people thought that imported wheat would be uneconomical and difficult to obtain. Inland firms ultimately decided not to relax easily due to the flood situation, so the market gradually became firm. However, the flow of current arrivals remains slow, so it is difficult for standard wheat to rise significantly. As a result, this month was 0.1 better than the previous day, August and September were 0.2 better, July was 0.3 better, November was 0.4 better, and December was 0.2 better. The spot wheat market remains flat. High-quality goods are priced at 5 qian, while mid-quality goods are priced between 0.2 and 0.3 qian. A total of 2,400+ bags of wheat from Kunshan, Danyang, Ben Niu, Shipu, Wangxianqiao, and Penglai were handled by Huafeng Fuxin.

Textiles: A Moveable Textile Market

Local Factory Cotton Cloth 194

The market has been quite firm recently, and spot goods of fine cloth are nearly exhausted. This is because, after the Sichuan firms searched the market, the inventories were already depleted. In addition, firms from Niuzhuang and Tianjin successively made purchases. However, there are no warehouse receipts for brands such as Laba Tong and Blue Chicken. Goods will arrive in two to three weeks. The shortage of spot goods is evident from this. Yanghe sold for 7 taels and 6 qian yesterday, and Hunter sold for 7 taels, 5 qian, and 2.5 fen. Fine twill has also been rising since the group was combined. Yanghe opened at 7 taels, 6 qian, and 5 fen, Blue Double Fish at 7 taels and 6 qian, and Squirrel at 7 taels and 1 qian and 5 fen. Coarse cloth sales are not sluggish.

Eastern and Western Textiles 195

There is a renewed momentum in actual sales. Customer firms are deeply concerned about a potential boycott, so they are eagerly purchasing eastern goods. Among them, Zhigong cloth is selling well. Tianjin firms purchased over 500 pieces of Sijunzi cloth. Hunting Goose and Sichuan firms are actively searching the market. Many Moganshan and Sanyoutu cloths were purchased by firms along the Yangtze River. The price rose by 0.025. Morris cloth has a large local volume, with Sanmatou priced at 2 taels, 8 qian, and 7.5 fen, and Sanggong priced at 2 taels, 7 qian, and 7.5 fen. However, Yuanyu silk is difficult to rise because the previously ordered goods are continuously arriving in Shanghai. Qingguan Mirror is priced at 12 taels and 1 qian, Bamboo Forest at 12 taels, and Santan at 11 taels, 9 qian, and 5 fen.

Silk and Tea Foreign Companies: Silk Sales Increasingly Lifeless 196

Yesterday, American silk sales remained stagnant. Silk prices declined. English and French silk sales were also sluggish. Yokohama silk prices fell sharply. Silk telegrams were not updated. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson only shipped five packages of Shanghai white factory silk, and Dachang shipped 15 packages of white dried silk. Prices remain flat and weak.

Wuxi Summer Cocoon Production Nearly Exhausted 197

Total Volume in the Entire County is Less Than 5,000 Dan

The summer cocoon production in Wuxi this year was initially smooth. The silkworms developed smoothly after hatching. However, during the critical period of the great sleep, continuous rain, combined with sultry heat and extreme cold, caused various silkworm diseases. Yellow diarrhea and black vomit were prevalent, and 80 to 90 percent were discarded. After the worms were put on the frames, they encountered severe thunderstorms, causing most of the silkworm moths to stop spinning silk. Many also died halfway. Cocoon production is nearly exhausted. The total volume for the entire county is estimated to be less than 5,000 dan. Only 20 to 30 percent of the cocoon merchants are formally opening scales. They are weighing and purchasing goods upon sight. The highest cocoon price is only 50 yuan. This year, the Wuxi summer cocoon market is nearly nonexistent.

Needle-Eyebrow Green Tea Sales to Europe Continue Smoothly 198

Yesterday, in the local foreign firms' tea market, needle-eyebrow green tea from Wuyuan and Tunxi, etc., was actively traded by firms like Xiehe, Longfu, and Tongfu, with brisk transactions. However, selling prices were slightly lower than before. The sale of precious eyebrow pearl tea of medium and low grades was also active, but the upper and middle-grade goods became sluggish. The Gongxi variety saw relatively active market conditions due to demand from Bombay indicated by telegrams to firms like Baitou, Zhuang Fulin, Qianyi, and Ruichang. However, because Russian firms have not yet started operations, it is difficult to stabilize the market.

Local News

Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Association Begins Economic Boycott of Japan 220

Finalizing the List of Committee Members

Banning Further Imports of Japanese Goods

Soliciting Boycott Proposals

Since the Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Congress resolved to vigorously implement an economic boycott of Japan, it has aroused sympathy and attention from all quarters. Yesterday, the association issued a warning prohibiting further imports of Japanese goods after the 14th. At the same time, the Municipal Federation of United Associations telegraphed to solicit economic boycott proposals for contribution. The list of committee members for the Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Association has now been finalized by the Municipal Party Headquarters, and the first meeting is scheduled to be held on the 17th. All measures will be actively carried out. The following is a record of the information obtained yesterday:

List of Committee Members 221

The Shanghai Municipal Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Committee was organized after a resolution by representatives from all walks of life in Shanghai. The list of committee members was also recommended by the Congress. However, for the sake of prudence, it was resolved on the spot to make a list of the recommended candidates and send it to the Municipal Party Headquarters for review and confirmation. Yesterday afternoon, the Municipal Party Headquarters convened a temporary executive committee meeting specifically for this matter and resolved: (1) The Municipal Party Headquarters will not participate in this organization in the name of a group; (2) The number of committee members will be changed to 37, including the Accountants Association; (3) The list of confirmed committee members is as follows: (Labor) Hou Dachun, Wang Wenhua, Wang Zhuping, Lu Jingshi, Li Yongxiang, Chen Peide, Tang Junsheng,

The Necessary Understanding and Effort Regarding the Anti-Chinese Incidents in Korea 222

1. Necessary Understanding: (1) The Wanbaoshan Incident was not only not the fuse for the anti-Chinese incidents in Korea, but was in fact a planned, organized, and step-by-step exploitation by Japanese imperialists as an active anti-Chinese movement. (2) The anti-Chinese sentiment of the Koreans was not out of their own volition, but was forced and threatened by Japanese imperialists to serve as a tool to oppress our overseas Chinese. (3) Japanese imperialists' aggression against our country is their consistent traditional policy in diplomacy. (4) Manchuria and Mongolia in the minds of the Japanese have long been the Japanese's Manchuria and Mongolia, not owned by our country.

2. Necessary Efforts: (1) The 400 million people of the country, under the leadership of the Chinese Kuomintang, must unite closely, and contact all oppressed nations and countries that sympathize with our country, and make a heroic and sworn resistance to the barbaric and arrogant Japanese imperialists. (2) Petition the Central Government to promptly organize an investigation committee to investigate the exact number of overseas Chinese killed and injured in this incident, and the total amount of property lost, and then demand compensation from the Japanese government within a time limit. (3) This time, the Japanese incited Korean people to排華 (anti-Chinese acts), lacking sincerity in protecting our overseas Chinese. In order to effectively ensure future safety, we should petition the National Government to send heavy troops to be stationed in Korea to protect us at any time. (4) Awaken the revolutionary consciousness of the Korean people, and together with our people, stand on the united front against imperialism, and fight to the death with Japanese imperialists. (5) The heads of the Japanese military police in Korea and the main culprits who caused the incident should be ordered to be severely punished by the Japanese government. (6) The people of all walks of life in this city should, under the leadership of our party, carry out a warm, lasting, and effective anti-Japanese movement. The economic boycott of Japan must be carried out uniformly in strict and proper steps. (7) Urge the Central Government to resolve this anti-Chinese incident in Korea through revolutionary diplomacy.

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang

Zhou Xuexiang, (Business) Wang Xiaolai, Zheng Chengqing, Wang Hanliang, Fang Jiaobo, Ye Huijun, Wang Yansong, Yu Qiaqing, Chen Songyuan, (Municipal Federation) Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, (Taxpayers Association) Hu Fengxiang, Cheng Zhusun, (National Goods Association) Wang Jie'an, Chen Xingzhuang, (Overseas Chinese Groups) Liu Shimu, Zhang Honghai, (Education Association) Tao Baichuan, Tong Xingbai, Feng Yixian, (Agriculture) Chen Yafu, Zhang Huijun, (Women's Groups) Lin Kecong, Wang Xiaoying, (Lawyers Association) Chen Tingrui, Li Cishan, (Press) Yan Esheng, Zhu Yingpeng, (Accountants Association) Xi Yushu, Li Wenjie, and appointed Hou Dachun, Wang Xiaolai, and Tao Baichuan as the conveners of the first meeting.

Scheduled Meeting 223

The conveners have decided that the first meeting will be held at 2:00 PM on the 17th of this month (Friday) in the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Standing Committee Room. It is also heard that Sun Mingqi, Xu Huimin, Tang Liqing, Li Ruzhang, etc., were also elected as members of the Congress. However, they all stated that their duties were繁劇 (numerous and onerous) and they had no time to spare. On the day after their election, they requested the Municipal Party Headquarters not to confirm them.

Important Warning 224

The Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Congress issued an important warning yesterday, stating that in accordance with the resolution of the Congress on the 13th of this month, an economic boycott of Japan will be vigorously implemented from today onwards. If anyone still privately imports Japanese goods after the 14th, once verified, the most severe sanctions will be imposed in accordance with the measures to be discussed in the future. This is a serious warning, and it is hoped that everyone will pay attention.

Circular Telegram to Various Industries 225

The association also sent a circular telegram to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and various industry associations in Shanghai yesterday, stating that the recent violent anti-Chinese incidents in various parts of Korea are actually a cunning scheme by the Japanese to organize and plan the invasion of Manchuria and Mongolia. They are using ignorant Korean people to destroy our shops and kill our overseas Chinese. The injured are lying everywhere, and it is unbearable to witness. According to telegrams, the property loss has exceeded ten million, and the number of overseas Chinese dead and injured is close to ten thousand. This is an unprecedented catastrophe for overseas Chinese, and a rare tragedy in the Republic of China. As the said Japanese imperialists, in order to relieve the domestic economic depression, do not hesitate to disregard the disapproval of the world, and disregard justice and humanity. Today, if the Japanese use economic relief as a motive, then we will use economic boycott as a shield. If the compatriots across the country arouse their conscience and rise up together and persevere to the end, the Japanese will eventually bow their heads, soften, and beg for peace. Therefore, the Congress resolved by the entire body to "permanently implement an economic boycott of Japan with a沉毅猛勇 (resolute and courageous) spirit." In particular, we respectfully inform all sectors to stop importing Japanese goods from today onwards. If any speculative奸商 (profiteering merchants) purchase Japanese goods again, they will be abandoning themselves to the people. Once the measures against Japan have been thoroughly discussed and agreed upon, this association will definitely impose severe sanctions. Please pay special attention to avoid being too late for regrets. [Signed] The Provisional Presidium of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Congress, Tao Baichuan, Wang Yansong, Zheng Chengqing, Wang Wenhua, Li Yongxiang [deleted].

Petition for Protection of Overseas Chinese 226

The association also sent a telegram petitioning the National Government to send troops to protect overseas Chinese, which reads: "To the National Government: We note that the Japanese used the Wanbaoshan Incident to incite Korean people to violently排華 (anti-Chinese acts), and dispatched military police to expand the riots. Overseas Chinese in Fushan, Seoul, Incheon, Zhennampo, Sinuiju, Kaesong, Wonsan, Sonchon, Kongju, Cheongju, Hwaseong, Gwangju, and other places in Korea have been brutally massacred, with more than ten thousand people killed. They treat our national sovereignty as if it does not exist, and discard world justice like worn-out shoes. Now, overseas Chinese are in great danger under this tyrannical oppression, and more than 90,000 people have not yet escaped. If we want to rely on Japanese police to maintain order, it is no different from negotiating with a tiger for its skin. Therefore, the Congress resolved to petition your government to: (1) strictly order the Northeast provincial governments to order all Japanese troops and police to leave the country within a time limit; (2) send troops to Korea to stop the riots and protect overseas Chinese. We implore you to consider the urgency of the situation and implement it quickly in order to alleviate the倒懸 (inverted hanging) and rescue the overseas Chinese from the deep waters and scorching fire. In haste, we await your orders with urgency." [Signed] The Provisional Presidium of the Shanghai Municipal Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Congress, Tao Baichuan, Wang Yansong, Zheng Chengqing, Wang Wenhua, Li Yongxiang [deleted].

Soliciting Proposals 227

The Shanghai Special District Municipal Federation telegraphed yesterday to solicit proposals for economic boycott of Japan, stating: "To all compatriots across the country: Since the Japanese incited Korean people to launch violent anti-Chinese incidents, our overseas Chinese have been displaced and killed, unable to return. The tragic situation cannot be described in words. Tracing the intentions of the暴日 (violent Japanese), on the one hand, they want to alienate the inherent feelings between the Chinese and Korean nations, and use the Korean people as the急先鋒 (vanguard) to actively invade Manchuria and Mongolia. On the other hand, they want to take the opportunity to destroy all the industry and commerce of overseas Chinese in Korea. Their intentions are clear to everyone. Our compatriots, grieving that the national crisis is imminent and lamenting the tragic massacre of overseas Chinese, must act promptly without delay. The Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Congress has resolved to organize a committee to carry out a sustained economic boycott of Japan. Our association will participate in it and cannot shirk its responsibility. Furthermore, in view of the shortcomings of previous economic boycotts of Japan, we should plan carefully and thoroughly before implementation. Therefore, we are issuing this circular telegram to solicit proposals, and we earnestly hope that all enlightened people across the country will share their wisdom and provide guidance. If there are detailed measures and implementation plans, we would be grateful if you would not hesitate to teach us before the 20th of this month and send them to this association at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce inside the Tianhou Palace Bridge堍 (bridge abutment), so that we can collect and discuss them and contribute them to the Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Committee for reference and adoption. To all the business compatriots across the country, the alarming situation should arouse your conscience and automatically resist. As the saying goes, "If a poisonous snake is in hand, a brave man will cut off his arm." Sacrificing one's limited interests is to leave a permanent life for future generations. In haste, we anxiously await your response." [Signed] The Shanghai Special District Municipal Federation [deleted].

Losses in Ramie Cloth 228

The ramie cloth industry leader, Liu Huanru, told a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter yesterday: "Among the regions in our country that produce ramie cloth, Jiangxi and Sichuan have the most, followed by Hunan, Chaozhou, and Suzhou. The total annual value is approximately 20 million yuan. Its largest market is Korea. Although it is subject to unreasonable oppression by the Korean customs, in recent years, the exports from Shanghai alone amount to approximately 4 million yuan for Jiangxi goods, 1 million yuan in total for Hunan and Sichuan goods, and 500,000 yuan in total for Chaozhou and Suzhou goods, totaling more than 5.5 million yuan. The peak sales period is June and July. Since the anti-Chinese riots occurred in Korea, we received telegrams just four days later to stop processing goods. In addition to direct and indirect losses, the intangible losses suffered by the seven major ramie cloth companies in the city, Hengshengdong, Deyu, Longhe, Tonghe Yong, Hejusheng, Yuantai, and Liuluji, etc., have already reached 300,000 yuan. The stock is piled up like mountains and has no market price. If this continues to be delayed, the losses will be even greater."

Request for Allocation of Funds 229

Various organizations in this city, during the anti-Japanese aid-to-overseas-Chinese rally held a few days ago, someone proposed that all the national salvation funds collected during the anti-Japanese association era should be remitted to Korea to aid the affected overseas Chinese compatriots. Upon hearing this, the organizations expressed deep sympathy. It is reported that the various organizations will jointly petition the central government and the city's party headquarters within days to immediately execute the remittance of all national salvation funds to Korea via telegraph to aid the overseas Chinese compatriots.

Yesterday, Two Military Organizations Held a Memorial Service for Hu Zuyu 231

Meeting in the morning, public memorial service in the afternoon

The Shanghai Garrison Headquarters and the Fifth Division's stationed troops in Shanghai held a memorial service for the late Division Commander of the Fifth Division, Hu Zuyu, at the Army Club on Jinji Road yesterday. The morning was a public memorial service for colleagues from the two organizations, and the afternoon was a public memorial service for all circles. Dozens of people attended, including Zhang Qun, Chen Xizeng, Yu Hongjun, Guo Waifeng, Wang Yunwu, Yuan Ludeng, Yang Hu, Zou Bingwen, and Wang Xiaolai, Yang Xiaotang, etc.

Venue Setup 232

The memorial service was held at the Army Club on Jinji Road. On both sides of the entrance and in the middle of the road, white cloth banners were horizontally inscribed with "Mourning General of the Army, Division Commander of the Fifth Division, Mr. Hu Deru." Inside the gate, the first thing was the signing area, and further inside, elegiac couplets from all walks of life were spread on both sides, interspersed with white lanterns. From a distance, it was all white as snow. In the center of the auditorium was Hu's portrait, and in the center of the table was a memorial tablet, with flowers, fruits, and sandalwood offerings in front, filling the room with incense. At the foot of the steps was the military band of the Garrison Department and the City Public Security Bureau, playing mourning music during the sacrifice.

Order of the Memorial Ceremony 233

The meeting began at nine o'clock in the morning. The military band of the Garrison Department played mourning music. A portion of the Fifth Division's stationed troops in Shanghai came in person to participate. The order of the memorial ceremony: (1) The officiant takes his place, the accompanying sacrificers take their places, stand in solemn respect; (2) Seventeen artillery salutes are fired; (3) Mourning music is played; (4) The most respectful salute is paid to the Party and National Flag, the portrait of the Prime Minister, and the memorial tablet of the late Division Commander Hu; (5) The eulogy is read; (6) Flowers are presented; (7) Three minutes of silence; (8) A report on the late Division Commander Hu's deeds and achievements; (9) Speeches; (10) Mourning music is played; (11) The ceremony is completed.

Reading the Eulogy 234

During the public memorial service, the Chief of Staff of the Garrison Department, Lai Weiying, officiated the memorial service for the late Division Commander Hu (photo taken by this newspaper)

Director Lai Weiying of the Garrison Department officiated, and Regiment Commander Zhou of the 26th Regiment of the Fifth Division and Regiment Commander Xie of the 27th Regiment were the accompanying sacrificers. Next, soldiers dispatched by the artillery company fired seventeen artillery salutes. Next, the officiant read the eulogy, saying: "On July 15th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, and Xu Jinyuan, Chief of Staff, leading all officers and men, and the various stationed troops of the Fifth Division in Shanghai, respectfully offer wine, libations, fragrant flowers, and humble delicacies, to pay tribute to the spirit of the late Division Commander of the Fifth Division, General Hu Deru, and say: 'Coming from Zhanggong, with Mount Lu in the north, the mountains and rivers are lush and deep, a place of loyalty and righteousness. Bright, bright Hu Gong, an outstanding talent of the era, with the tolerance of the sea and the earth, and the stability of a mountain and abyss. Giving up embroidery, he did not engage in rhetoric. Studying in Baoyang, he researched military classics. Learning for practical application, he joined the army. Exhausting his energy and showing his talent like a leopard, he was compared to a soaring dragon. Oh, magnificent Sun Gong, rising in the south, following with a crossbow, wandering ten thousand miles, falling and rising repeatedly, unyielding in a hundred setbacks. For fifteen years, the campaign was launched. He first pacified the Jiangxi border and then stabilized Fujian. His spirit was as strong as mountains and rivers, his formation was like monkeys and birds. In years of battles, he did not take off his battle clothes. North and South of the Yangtze River, East and West of the Huai River, with the major enemies eliminated, stationed in Wumen. Unfazed by seven offerings, and the bandits were awed. Praised for his merits and rewards, he was recommended as a division commander. Aides and soldiers were all cheering. The stupid red bandits, wantonly wreaked havoc in the south of the Yangtze River, Heaven’s punishment has been delayed for long, and both gods and men are angry. Ordered to suppress bandits, he was brave and went to the front. Ten attacks, ten decisive battles, the stubborn enemies collapsed. Pacifying the good and eliminating the evil, he fought in Guangchang, vowing to wipe out the ugly kind. Stabilizing the homeland, the evil aura was pressing, and a general fell. Alas, a great hero, died halfway with regret. The bow and sword sadly wailed, the heavens and earth sank into gloom. The three armies shed blood, and the seven elite were heartbroken. His meritorious service in defending was high, the ceremony of honoring the dead was important. The Taichang inscribed his merits, praying for a tomb at Qilian. Alas, Hu Gong, born in glory and dying in sorrow, his fragrance remains in the history books. Rest in peace in the underworld. Shihui is not talented, and shared the same boat in adversity. Recalling his heroism, tears flow horizontally. The white sun is bleak, the blue sky is vast. May his spirit come and enjoy these three cups. Farewell.'

Hu's Deeds 235

The Garrison Department's Staff Officer Zhong then reported on Hu Zuyu's deeds and achievements, saying: "Hu Gong came from a very poor family. At a young age, he entered the Jiangxi Military Primary School to study. He studied diligently, and his conduct was the best in the whole school. Soon, he encountered the Xinhai Revolution. He followed the former Governor Ma Gong in the Jiujiang Campaign. After things were settled, he returned to school. After graduation, he entered the Hubei Preparatory School and the Baoding Military Academy. After completing his studies, he was assigned to the Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief of the Upper Yangtze River as a trainee and company commander. Because his principles differed from those in power, he was depressed and resigned, going to Guangdong and serving under the former Commander of the 14th Army, Commander Lai, serving as company and battalion commander. He fought in Guangdong, Guangxi, Fujian, and Jiangxi, and was known for his bravery. The former 14th Army Commander Lai's troops were reorganized into the Fourth Division of the Jiangxi Army. He secretly contacted the revolutionary army, and Hu Gong and the late First Division Commander Yi Gong really approved of his plan. In the Northern Expedition of the 15th year, he made great contributions in the battles of Jishui and Fuzhou, and was promoted to regimental commander. Afterwards, he entered Zhejiang from Fujian, reaching Yixing. In the battle of Zhangzhu, he defeated Bai Baoshan's 30,000 troops. He then captured Changzhou, cutting off the Shanghai-Nanjing transportation, and his merits were especially great. In the Northern Expedition of the 16th year, he participated in the battles of Jiangyin and Jingjiang, and the battle of Linyi, Shandong. He led his troops to bravely climb the city. Later, due to the loss of the main force in Xuzhou, the entire army retreated. Hu Gong led a regiment to cover the rear, and the enemy dared not pursue. In the Second Northern Expedition of the 17th year, he served as deputy division commander, leading his troops across the river. In the battle of Jining Jiajiazhuang, his arrangements were meticulous, and the Japanese army did not dare to invade. After things were settled, he returned to Suzhou and Shanghai to appease the local area, and his efforts were especially appreciated. In the 18th year, Bao Gang and Shi Yousan successively rebelled. He led his troops to pursue and attack, and the enemies were completely routed. Returning to Suzhou, he was appointed as the Commander-in-Chief for Suppressing Bandits in Taihu Lake. After months of hard work, the bandits in the lake were eliminated. In the 19th year, Yan Feng's disturbances occurred, and he led his division to suppress the rebellion. In the Guide and Minquan areas, he fought fiercely with the enemy, greatly appreciated by the commander-in-chief. After the war ended, he was promoted to division commander, entered Jiangxi to suppress the Reds, and eliminated the bandits in northeastern Jiangxi. The local people praised him endlessly. When pursuing and suppressing the bandits in Nanfeng and Guangchang, he went deep with his isolated army and won victories repeatedly. But because he personally directed from a high ground, he was shot and died. From then on, the loyal and brave Division Commander Hu was permanently separated from us, which was the greatest loss for the Party and the country. (There is also a letter from the Special Party Department of the Fifth Division to all circles, the words of which are omitted.)"

Summary of the Speech 236

Then, the Deputy Brigade Commander Zhou of the 26th Regiment gave a speech, saying: "The deeds of Hu Gong have already been reported. I have many feelings at the memorial service, and I am especially grieved. I have been with him for more than ten years, sharing life and death, and I feel that Hu Gong's knowledge and conduct are sufficient to be a model for soldiers. His failure to suppress the bandits is a major loss for the Party and the country. We can only lead the brave soldiers to personally exterminate the bandits in order to avenge him and comfort Hu Gong in the underworld," etc.

The meeting began to adjourn around 11 o'clock. From 2 o'clock in the afternoon, representatives from all walks of life arrived and offered sacrifices, and cars clogged the roads, which were extremely crowded.

Foreign Ship Pilots in Shanghai Demand Increased Fees 237

But the consular body and others do not agree with the request

The situation of confrontation between the two sides is serious

When foreign merchant ships arrive in Shanghai, they must be guided into the port by pilots after arriving at Wusong. Because foreign ship owners are not familiar with the situation of the Bund in the Huangpu River, they must rely on the guidance of pilots. However, the right to pilot ships in Shanghai has been controlled by foreigners for decades. The pilots have an association, located at No. 26 on the Bund. All the more than twenty pilots are Westerners. It is reported that there is only one Chinese pilot. The pilotage fee is very high. Generally, for a ship of more than 5,000 tons, the pilotage fee for entering and leaving Shanghai once is about 600 taels. For example, the Changxing Empress ship needs to pay more than 1,000 taels for pilotage fees for entering and leaving the port once. Now, the pilots, due to the rising gold prices and the high cost of living, specifically convened a general meeting on the 14th, demanding that the shipping companies increase the pilotage fees. When reporters heard the news, they immediately inquired with the association, but they strictly kept it secret. Yesterday, they specifically went to various parties to inquire and learned about the general situation as follows:

Request to Increase Fees 238

The Foreign Ship Pilot Association, on the evening of October 4th

Page 14

At 3:00 PM, convened all pilots to discuss the issue of increasing pilotage fees. The reason is that the price of gold is soaring and the cost of living is increasing. Compared with other countries in the world, China's pilotage fee is the shortest. They requested that the shipping companies appropriately increase the currently set fee by 20 percent. For example, from 500 taels per time, increase to 600 taels. The association submitted the request to the shipping companies.

The Shipping Companies Disagree 239

The collection of pilotage fees cannot directly collect money from the shipping bureaus according to the established practice. The association must issue a receipt, and then send it to the Shanghai Consular Body, the British Chamber of Commerce, and the Jianghai Customs, etc., for joint signature before the shipping companies can collect the money. This has been the procedure in the past. Now that the pilots are asking for an increase in fees, they must also follow this method and first pass the consular body, the British Chamber of Commerce, etc., before it can be effective. Yesterday, it was heard that the consular body and the British Chamber of Commerce expressed their disagreement with this fee increase proposal, so the shipping companies unanimously rejected it.

Temporary Work Stoppage 240

Starting at 3:00 PM on the 14th, the pilots stopped working in order to attend the meeting. The ships from Europe, America, and Japan arriving in Shanghai were not guided into the port after arriving at Wusong, so eight foreign ships were blocked. Until yesterday morning, the pilots, in accordance with the association's order, resumed work as usual, stating that the conditions had been put forward. The British ships blocked in Wusong, such as the Xuefubo Mai, Ping Erda, and the German ship Yadu, etc., were guided into the port by the pilots at noon and were already unloading cargo as usual. The outgoing ships also departed yesterday. They were blocked for more than ten hours.

What Was Heard from the Discussion 241

Yesterday afternoon, the reporter specifically went to the association to inquire about everything, but the association strictly kept the matter secret, saying that the Westerners in the meeting knew about it and it was not convenient to inform. Thus, the reporter did not get the main points. The reporter went to the shipping bureaus to inquire about everything. The shipping companies were not very clear about the attitude of the Pilot Association. However, according to what was heard, if there is no satisfactory reply today, the pilots will take the most serious and decisive measures. It is feared that this will cause ships to be blocked from entering and leaving the Huangpu River at that time.

The Shipping Companies' Attitude 242

The reporter also inquired about the claims of the shipping companies from all sides. In general, they cannot hastily agree to the fee increase, because it must be agreed by the three organizations. If the pilots take decisive measures, the shipping companies have also discussed a kind of remedial plan. Before the matter is realized, it cannot be revealed. However, the method is to maintain the ships and not stop them as the main thing.

Chinese Ships Are Not Affected 243

Chinese merchant ships have always hired their own pilots. Whether it is a ship on the Yangtze River or in the South or North Seas, each ship has a pilot assigned. Therefore, the current turmoil in foreign pilotage, even if a strike is realized, will not hinder Chinese ships at all.

Dawan Daily reports that regarding the revision of the pilotage fee, the Inspector General of Customs summoned the River Affairs Department and the Patrol Engineering Department this morning (15th) for an important discussion. It ended at noon, and the contents could not be ascertained. It is reported that the Pilot Association requested that the pilotage fee be changed to gold coins for calculation and paid in silver taels. One Shanghai standard silver tael is at least equivalent to one shilling and eight pence, and at most equivalent to two shillings and three pence. According to the new price, it is about 20 percent higher than the current price. It is also heard that the current licensed pilots earn about 1,300 taels per month. After deducting various expenses, they can actually get 900 taels. As for the attitude of the shipping companies, because their current business is depressed, they all believe that it is not yet time to increase fees.

Xinming Ship Raises Fire and Waits for Departure 244

Waiting for a telegram back from Yantai, Korea

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming ship, upon receiving a telegram order from the Ministry of Communications, was sent to Korea to transport the distressed overseas Chinese back to the country. The bureau has prepared food and materials and is waiting for a reply telegram from Yantai, Korea, before opening. It was originally planned to export it yesterday afternoon. General Manager Guo of the bureau believed that since the Xinming was going to Korea, the bureau had no pier, and matters such as importing, stopping, checking ship money, etc., must be negotiated in advance to avoid accidents. Therefore, the night before, he specifically telegraphed the Consul General in Seoul, Zhang Weicheng, asking him to handle it on his behalf, and inquired whether the ship needed to go to Korea, and stated that he would wait for a reply telegram to Shanghai before opening. At the same time, he sent a third telegram to the Yantai Chamber of Commerce, asking again if the previous two telegrams had been received and why there was no reply. He asked whether the Xinming's return to Korea to rescue overseas Chinese compatriots would return to Yantai or other ports, and asked them to telegraph quickly so that Xinming could be informed. However, after the two telegrams were sent, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company waited for telegrams from the two places. Until yesterday afternoon, no reply telegrams had been received, so the Xinming ship had not yet departed. However, the bureau still ordered the Xinming to stop at the Jinliyuan pier, waiting for the reply telegrams from Korea and Yantai to arrive, before sailing. If the telegram arrives at night, the ship can depart this morning.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Issues Back Pay to Ship Crew and Sailors 245

Pay in full monthly from now on

The salaries of the stewards, stokers, and sailors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ships were in arrears during the time of the former General Manager Zhao Tieqiao. When Li Zhonggong took office and the current commissioner Guo Waifeng succeeded him, the stewards, stokers, and sailors on each ship had been in arrears for three or four months, causing great difficulties in the lives of the crew and sailors. Since Commissioner Guo took office, he has been deeply concerned about the hardships of the employees on the ships and the importance of their work at sea. Therefore, on May 12, he first paid two or three months of the back pay. Then, the back pay for April, May, and June was paid in full the day before yesterday. From now on, they will be paid monthly without further delay. The three types of employees on each ship were very grateful for this. They specifically elected Chairman Che Defang of the Junan Association as their representative to express the sincerity of all the stewards, stokers, and sailors to Commissioner Guo. Guo was very pleased with Che's enthusiasm for the bureau's affairs, which he had been doing for decades as if it were one day, and said that the salaries of the crew and stokers would be paid on time every month from now on, and there would be no further delays. This time, in the midst of economic difficulties, priority was given to raising the arrears of the crew, so that the lives of the sailors would not be affected and they could work with peace of mind.

The Bureau of Health Intensifies Epidemic Prevention Work 249

Personnel will be sent to foreign ships at the port to inspect.

The Shipping Association requests exemption for passengers on Shanghai-Ningbo ships.

The Municipal Bureau of Health, because it is the summer season when infectious diseases are prone to occur, the city's prevention and control should be intensified. In addition to paying special attention to public food and street cleaning, epidemic prevention stations are also set up everywhere to prepare for emergencies. Recently, the bureau has also received news from places such as India that cases of cholera and meningitis have been found. It is deeply feared that travelers will spread the diseases inland. In order to ensure thorough prevention, the bureau plans to send personnel to inspect foreign ships before landing. If there are indeed serious cases of the disease, they will either be sent to the hospital for treatment or prevented from landing. If the cases are lighter, personnel sent by the Bureau of Health will provide appropriate treatment to prevent the spread and eliminate the occurrence. According to Zhong Zhiqi, section chief of the Bureau of Health, the entire inspection plan is currently being studied and planned.

The Shanghai Shipping Association sent a letter to the National Seaport Quarantine Office yesterday, saying, "Respectfully, the members of the shipping companies China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Sanbei Shipping Company, and Ning Shao Shipping Company sent letters saying that they received a letter from the National Seaport Inspection Office approving a letter from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Health requesting cooperation in dispatching officials to inspect passengers coming from Ningbo to Shanghai by ship, and to forcibly inject cholera prevention needles to passengers in steerage. They were instructed to report vessels coming from Ningbo 24 hours before entry so that personnel can be dispatched for inspection. It is noted that the water route between Shanghai and Ningbo is close, and the ship schedule is frequent, departing in the evening and arriving in the morning, arriving early and departing late. When there are the most passengers, including the crew, the number is more than 3,000. If cholera prevention needles are to be injected by name and stools are collected, it is impossible to complete during the journey from Song to Shanghai (the ship travels from Song to Shanghai in less than an hour). If the ship has arrived in Shanghai Port, but the inspection procedures have not yet been completed and passengers are prohibited from landing, then the large number of people will be difficult to contain. If enforcement is strengthened, it will cause trouble. Therefore, the result is sufficient to hinder transportation and affect business. It is difficult in fact and has a major relationship. In any case, it is difficult to comply with. We should request the association to forward the letter to cancel the practice of inspecting passenger stools and forcibly injecting cholera prevention needles on ships from Ningbo, in order to facilitate transportation and maintain the shipping industry. We are sincerely committed to public relations." Another letter to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Health, the text of which is omitted.

Wu Song Quarantine Hospital Inspects Sailing Vessels 250

All Vessels Infected with Plague

Must Undergo Fumigation

The Wu Song Pao Taiwan Public Quarantine Hospital, along with Western-trained doctors Hu Junhe from Hubei and Chen from Shantou, recognizing the prevalence of plague in ports like Hong Kong, have taken measures to safeguard Shanghai by inspecting cargo sailing vessels susceptible to the disease. Special attention is being given to live pig boats arriving in Shanghai from various Jiangbei ports. Therefore, all pig boats entering the port must anchor off the Pao Taiwan shore for inspection. When the doctors board for inspection, if giant rats are found in the cargo hold, quarantine procedures must be followed, including spraying the holds with disinfectant and fumigating them with sulfur smoke, saltpeter, and various medicinal powders. Only after completing the fumigation are the vessels allowed to proceed to Shanghai. The fumigation fee is ten taels of silver per vessel, to be paid by the shipowners.

Biyuan Red Cross Branch Appeals for Disaster Relief via Telegram 251

The Chinese Red Cross Society recently received another telegram from the Biyuan Branch in Henan, appealing for disaster relief. It stated that people are without clothing, food, or shelter, and their cries for help go unheard. Several come to the branch for assistance every day, their starving and dying state truly unbearable to hear and see. These victims are like fish stranded in a dry rut, needing water from the West River to be saved. Due to the branch's lack of funds, even with the utmost charity and enthusiasm, it is powerless to address the situation. Currently, the branch is providing clothing, food, medicine, burials, and infant care, relying on donations from the slightly more affluent members to maintain the status quo. However, a drizzle cannot revive withered seedlings, and a single tree cannot support a large building. Furthermore, the increase in bandit activity threatens to leave no survivors in Tang County, making the situation even more unbearable. The Red Cross Society is actively preparing for disaster relief, and once funds are available, they will be submitted to the Standing Committee for review.

Police Recover Another Car

Shuai Rode in This Car After Kidnapping Lu

Defendant Still Firmly Denies Involvement

Shuai Songping, aka "Shuai the Bearded," a former high-ranking official turned kidnapper, was apprehended by the police for kidnapping Lu Shaotang, a comprador at the Banque de l'Indochine, and demanding ransom. He was handed over to the Special District Court for interrogation, as previously reported. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Jia-shi of the Criminal Court conducted a further hearing. Ren Zhennan Not Prosecuted for Indecent Assault 253

Lawyer Ren Zhennan was accused by his wife in the District Court of indecent behavior. After investigation by the prosecutor, he was not prosecuted. The details are of interest to those concerned with social and legal issues, and the full text is recorded below.

Defendant 254

Ren Zhennan, male, 23 years old, from Guangdong, lawyer, residing at 16 Beile Road, Shanghai.

Facts 255

Jiang Xingjuan, i.e., Ren Jiang's, accused the defendant of acting perversely and inhumanely, causing serious injury to her anus, and requested investigation and punishment. The plaintiff stated that she is 21 years old and was betrothed to the defendant as a child bride at the age of 13. They were formally married on May 10 of this year. The defendant, after frequenting brothels and contracting a venereal disease, passed bloody urine. On the third day of their marriage, he attempted anal sex, attempting it over ten times. He often could not penetrate, causing unbearable pain. When he could not penetrate, he often beat her, causing pain in her private area. Two weeks prior, he managed to penetrate her anus twice, causing injury and bleeding. An examination showed no injuries to her head, face, chest, abdomen, or genitalia, only a minor bluish-red bruise on her left leg caused by a kick.

Reasoning 256

According to legal principles, the definition of crime and punishment is governed by law. Any act punishable by law is a crime and cannot be analogized or inferred. Therefore, Article 1 of China's Criminal Law states that there can be no crime without a specific law. In this case, the victim and the defendant were formally married on May 10, and according to Article 1001 of the Civil Code, they have an obligation to cohabit. Therefore, the crimes of indecent behavior in Article 241, forced act in Article 318, and rape in Article 240 of the Criminal Law are not applicable. Although Chapter 2 of Part 4 of the Civil Code does not provide specific rules on how to fulfill the obligation to cohabit, if intercourse between husband and wife causes significant harm, it cannot be considered a crime. Similarly, there is no explicit law prohibiting anal intercourse. Indecency towards women should be punished by education and morality, not by criminal law. Regarding the injury to the left leg, the element of injury in criminal law requires damage to the physiological function of the human body. In other words, it must impair the function of the body. Domestic quarrels and violence are common. Although the kick caused a minor bluish-red bruise, it did not reach the level of impairing function. Even if the allegations are true, it is only a violation of police regulations and not punishable under Article 293, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Moreover, harmony is valued in the family. Even if there are disputes, seeking resolution through the Civil Code is more practical. For minor injuries, it is inappropriate to impose criminal punishment. Therefore, in accordance with Article 244, Paragraph 2 and 3 of the Criminal Procedure Law, no prosecution will be initiated. Liu Maochu, Chief Prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court, July 14, 1931.

Inheritance Dispute of Pang Qingcheng 257

Nephew Sues Uncle for Failure to Fulfill Contract

After the death of Pang Qingcheng, a wealthy man from Nanxun, his family held an estate division, dividing the property into three shares. Two shares went to Qingcheng's sons, Bingquan and Qingchen, and one share went to Qingcheng's brother, Laichen. Each share was worth about 190,000 yuan. In addition, real estate worth 50,000 yuan was designated for ancestral worship. The remaining public hall property worth over 200,000 yuan was managed by Pang Laichen. It was also divided into three shares, and it was decided that within eight weeks after January 9, 1929, accountants would be appointed to work with Pang Tiansheng and other managers to liquidate the assets. A contract was drawn up, but for over two years, Pang Laichen has failed to fulfill the contract. Pang Bingquan then hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to sue Pang Laichen in the Special District Court, requesting a judgment ordering him to fulfill the contract and hand over all public hall property accounts for liquidation. Judge Zhou Daren of the Civil Court Nine summoned the defendant yesterday morning, but he did not appear. Lawyers Zhu Sifu and Cai Nipei appeared on his behalf. Lawyer Zhu stated that the defendant, Pang Laichen, went to Beiping on April 22 and has not returned. Therefore, the lawyers were only entrusted by his family and have not received a power of attorney signed by him. He also stated that there was hope for a settlement and requested a two-week adjournment, which Judge Zhou granted. The court was then adjourned.

Appeal of Drug Trafficking Case Opens 258

Arguments Concluded by Both Sides

Court Orders Sentencing at a Later Date

Jieji Company at 146 Taoyuanfang, Beihainan Road, specializes in freight transportation. On March 23 of this year, Yu Zhenxiang, the company's accountant and manager, brought 362 packages from an unknown location and loaded them onto a truck, intending to send them to Shanxi, Hebei, and other places via the Jiangwan Post Office. While passing Beisichuan Road, the truck was stopped by Chief Inspector Lu Jiankui and detective Zhang Shaoqing of the General Inspectorate. Upon searching, the 362 packages were found to contain narcotics such as red pills, morphine, and heroin. Both the goods and Yu and his accomplice Li Hongru were arrested and handed over to the Special District Court for sentencing. Yu was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 3,000 yuan, while Li was sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined 1,000 yuan. The narcotics were confiscated. Yu, dissatisfied with the verdict, appealed to the Higher Branch Court. Yesterday morning, presiding judge Song Yuan and associate judges Du and Gao held a hearing. Lawyer Zhang Tianyin represented the police, while lawyers Zheng Wenkai, Xue Jiaqi, and Wang Zuxun represented Yu. Judge Song first questioned the witness Li Hongru briefly and then ordered arguments. Lawyer Zheng and others stated that the initial sentence was entirely based on Li Hongru's testimony. However, after careful review of Li's testimony, inconsistencies were found, and today's testimony differed from the initial testimony, making it unreliable. They requested that Yu be declared innocent. They also stated that Yu was ill in prison and requested that he be released on bail. Police lawyer Zhang stated that if the appellant requested a reduced sentence, the police might agree, but a request for acquittal was inappropriate both in law and in equity. He requested a ruling. Judge Song then declared the arguments concluded and scheduled sentencing for a later date.

Explanation of the Weights and Measures Inspection Office's Implementation of the New System 265

The Shanghai Weights and Measures Inspection Office, in response to a submission from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce based on resolutions from its members' representative assembly, requesting the adoption of four measures for implementing the new weights and measures system, submitted a response to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau clarifying misunderstandings. The Social Affairs Bureau then approved the response and forwarded it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating: "Received and forwarded to the Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Office for review. The response states: "After reviewing the points raised by the members' representatives, there appears to be a misunderstanding of the meaning and implementation of the new system. The weights and measures within the city are being standardized simultaneously, not sequentially. The inspection schedule is merely the order of operations, not a sequential order of standardization. This is the first point. Periodic inspections of weights and measures are conducted annually according to regulations. Shanghai, as a commercial and industrial city, will begin implementation in 1931, as delaying further would prevent universal inspection within a year. While it is true that delaying inspections would allow merchants to prepare adequately, the office estimates that the production capacity of weights and measures manufacturers in the city is sufficient to meet the needs of merchants and residents at any time, preventing shortages. Furthermore, the office's inspections are conducted by district and period. For example, the Hubei district is designated as the first period, the Zhabei district as the second period, and the Special District as the third period. The first period is scheduled from July 11 to September 16. Therefore, during the inspection of Hubei, Zhabei can prepare, and during the inspection of Zhabei, the Special District can prepare. The long duration between these periods allows for sufficient preparation. Even within the first district, Hubei, the police precincts of the Public Safety Bureau are divided into seven zones, allowing merchants to prioritize preparation based on the order of inspections. This is the second point. Regarding penalties during inspections, the office does not plan to strictly enforce them this year, and is under strict orders to comply. Therefore, the implementation period is essentially a promotional period. However, explicitly defining the promotional period may conflict with regulations. This is the third point. The chamber requested that representatives from trade associations participate in inspections. The department's inspection regulations do not include such a provision, and it appears that no exceptions should be made. Furthermore, the stated goal of preventing harassment is based on a misunderstanding. Inspection officers have the legal authority to conduct inspections with the assistance of police officers. If an officer is truly intent on harassment, trade association representatives would be unable to stop them. Moreover, under national law, the officer would be subject to criminal penalties. Article 11 of the department's inspection regulations clearly outlines the penalties for violations by inspection officers. This is the fourth point. The office only destroys weights and measures that are beyond repair. Items that can be repaired are not included. Regarding the request to allow merchants to temporarily use old weights and measures before purchasing new ones, the office believes that merchants should submit a guarantee to the office and its subordinate public security agencies, promising to purchase new weights and measures within a certain number of days and send the old weights and measures to the office to be stamped as invalid. This would be a more equitable and legal solution." Therefore, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau approved this reply for the information of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. This concludes the order.

Customs Report on Chinese and Foreign Commerce for Last Year 266

Imports Valued at 68 Million Taels

Rice and Wheat Account for 16.4 Million Taels

Exports Decrease by 51 Million Taels

The Inspectorate General of Customs released its report on Chinese and foreign commerce for 1930 yesterday. The main points of the report show that China's total imports were valued at 68 million Haikwan taels, an increase of 9% compared to the previous year. Exports decreased by 51 million taels, or 14%. Surprisingly, for a country known as an agricultural nation, imports of rice, wheat, and other grains reached 16.4 million Haikwan taels. Total customs revenue for the country was approximately 18.06 million Haikwan taels. Shanghai accounted for 51% of the country's imports and 35% of its exports. Shanghai's silver reserves were 105 million taels in the spring, 173 million yuan, 109 million taels in the summer, 153 million yuan, 105 million taels in the autumn, 137 million yuan, and 96 million taels in the winter, 143 million yuan. Silver imports came from the United States (46,938,845 ounces), Great Britain (3,546,248 ounces), Japan (2,329,539 ounces), and other countries (3,510,028 ounces), for a total of 56,324,659 ounces, less than half the previous year.

Feng Zhushi Requests Overseas Cantonese to Raise Funds for Guangdong Flood Relief 270

All Shores of the Three Rivers Have Become Marshland

Flood Victims are Everywhere, No Relief is Heard Of

The Guomin She (National Citizen Society) reports that the eastern, western, and northern rivers of Guangdong Province have simultaneously experienced torrential floods. All areas along the shores have turned into marshlands. The severity of the disaster is unprecedented in the last decade or so, yet there has been no word of overseas Cantonese raising funds for relief. Currently, Feng Zhushi, a Cantonese residing in Shanghai, has specially written to the Guangzhao Public Association, Chaozhou Guild Hall, and other organizations, requesting them to quickly organize relief efforts. The original letter is transcribed below.

Respectfully stated: Yesterday, reading the newspaper, it was reported that continuous rainfall in Guangdong Province in recent months has caused torrential floods in the eastern, western, and northern rivers simultaneously, resulting in a major flood disaster, unheard of in the last ten-odd years. This is the second flood disaster in the Dongjiang (East River) this time. It is found that in Huiyang, Boluo, Heyuan, and other counties, the water depth has increased from over two feet to over twenty feet. In slightly lower-lying areas, it has reached a staggering fifty to sixty feet, a vast expanse of water where no grass is seen. The lower reaches of the Dongjiang, with the lowest terrain, have more than ten water lanes along the city, which are already several feet deep. The water level of the Chao, Mei, and Han rivers has also risen by more than six feet. The Xijiang (West River) has also been rising steadily in recent days, with the western floods also rising sharply. Many areas along the Xijiang have been flooded. Currently, from Zhaoqing Gorge to the downstream, the water depth is over ten feet. Shijiao Enclosure is on the verge of collapse, fortunately, nearby residents are making great efforts to rescue it, thus avoiding the disaster. However, the upstream water is turbulent and swift as an arrow, with surging waves. From Shijiao Enclosure to Lubao, the water and sky are the same color, boundless and indistinct. Many of the embankments along the way have been flooded, and countless houses have been washed away. Observing the current water situation, it continues to rise. The flooding in Sanshui this year is not far from that of the year of Yimao (i.e., the fourth year of the Republic, 1915). If it continues to rain heavily during the day, the embankments will inevitably collapse beyond salvation. Currently, the Lubao Dapu Enclosure has already been breached by dozens of feet due to unsuccessful rescue efforts. The overwhelming water has buried all the ripening sorghum and early rice, creating an unprecedentedly huge flood disaster in Guangdong Province. The embankments that have not yet collapsed are in imminent danger.

The area along the Beijiang (North River) is particularly severely affected. From Yingde and below, in places like Boluokeng, Lianjiang, Lidong, Hengshi, and Pajiang, the floods have overflowed, turning everything into marshland. The lowest-lying areas are flooded to a depth of over twenty feet, with the shallowest being seven or eight feet or more. Therefore, the houses in the villages have all been submerged to the rooftops, and countless have collapsed as a result. Hundreds of thousands of people in the disaster area have all fled to the nearby mountains, sleeping in the open air and exposed to the wind and rain. Epidemics are spreading, and many have fallen ill and died as a result. Livestock and vegetables are floating on the water surface, which is a heartbreaking sight. Even if the floodwaters recede, the signs of famine have already formed. This time, the disaster area is vast, and the disaster is extremely severe. Hundreds of thousands of disaster victims who have escaped to the mountains and fields are crying out for food. However, the local authorities here have not heard any plans for relief. Although I, a humble fellow villager, have the heart but not the strength, in a state of panic, I hereby respectfully inform fellow villagers of Guangdong Province everywhere. I earnestly request that you quickly rise up together to organize relief efforts to save hundreds of thousands of fellow villagers from dire straits. Painful words of appeal, I humbly hope for your attention.

Respectfully, Feng Zhushi, a Cantonese residing in Shanghai.

Resolution of Treatment Conditions for Silk Throwing Industry 273

Both Parties Agree to Sign Nine Articles

The workers in the Shanghai silk throwing industry have put forward eleven conditions in order to improve their treatment. After mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau, yesterday was the final mediation date. Fortunately, both parties agreed and signed a resolution. The original text of the conditions is recorded as follows:

The labor and management of the silk throwing industry have jointly agreed on the following treatment conditions:

Article 1: The management recognizes the union's right to represent its members.

Article 2: The working hours are stipulated as eight hours. If the factory's working hours exceed the stipulated time, the workers must be paid additional wages of 500 wen for male workers and 200 wen for female workers per hour, and so on. If it does not exceed thirty minutes, half the amount will be paid.

Article 3: Each stand shall be set up with one foreman, who shall manage the work under the direction of the management. If there are several foremen in a row, one of them shall be elected as the leader.

Article 4: The foreman shall not concurrently perform martial arts work. When female workers serve as foremen, their wages must be paid according to the wages of male foremen.

Article 5: The management shall not dismiss workers without reason. If there is a serious mistake that requires dismissal, the union must be notified in advance.

Article 6: When the management hires new workers, it must give priority to hiring unemployed members of the union. However, these unemployed members must be approved by the government after review.

Article 7: If a worker falls ill while working, the management must pay the full day's wage in addition to declaring leave of absence.

Article 8: For national government-stipulated commemorative festivals, work shall be temporarily allowed for half a day, and wages shall be paid for the full day.

Article 9: These conditions shall take effect from the date of signing.

Preferential Treatment for Female Postal Service Examinations 274

The Postal Workers' Union Holds a Skeptical Attitude

It is reported that the Ministry of Communications has ordered the Postal Administration to give preferential consideration to female candidates in the upcoming recruitment of postal workers. There has been much speculation about this. According to sources from the local Postal Workers' Union, the post office began hiring female employees last year. However, the principle of equal opportunity for men and women was adopted during the examinations, and the same treatment was given to all, regardless of gender, only considering academic qualifications. There has never been any distinction between preferential or inferior treatment. The Ministry of Communications' opinion on giving preferential consideration to women in the recruitment, as reported this time, is not found in the official documents. Whether it is true or not remains to be proven. In short, the method of preferential recruitment clearly violates the meaning of "equality". Our government, which emphasizes harmony and equality, will never make such a special and strange move. In order to maintain the spirit of equality, we very much hope that this move will not be realized. It is also heard that the executive committee of the union decided yesterday to formally ask the ministry to explain the reasons after the news is confirmed.

Twin-Cocoon Silk Factories Share Public Debt Rights 278

There are a total of 106 silk factories in Shanghai, including 6 twin-cocoon silk factories and 100 single-cocoon silk factories. There is also one twin-cocoon silk factory in Zhejiang and Hangzhou. This time, the silk factory operators in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have jointly applied to the government for the issuance of 8 million yuan of silk industry public debt, with 4 million yuan for improving silk machinery and 4 million yuan for subsidizing silk factory operations. All issues related to the allocation of debt quotas and the management of funds have been carried out by specialized committees. However, the nature of twin-cocoon silk factories and single-cocoon silk factories are different, and the ministry intends to not allow them to enjoy the rights of public debt equally. The Shanghai Silk Factory Association considers that twin-cocoon silk factories are also members of the association and should not be discriminated against. Chairman Shen has repeatedly argued with reason at the executive committee meeting of the special committee. It has now been resolved that twin-cocoon silk factories will also enjoy the rights of public debt, with the same treatment as single-cocoon silk factories. It has been requested that the Ministry of Finance order the Jianghai Customs to collect special taxes on the export of twin-cocoon silk from now on. The special taxes on the export of twin-cocoon silk before should be made up for according to the amount.

National Product Commercial Field Case 279

The information heard yesterday is summarized below:

Municipal Government Notice 280

The original text of the notification letter from the Municipal Government Secretariat to the field stated: "Notification of matters, regarding the case of the National Product Commercial Field being sealed up, there are questions to be asked. It is hoped that representatives will be sent to the office to wait for inquiries at 3:00 PM on the 17th of this month. Injury Case Judgment 283

On the evening of June 10th, at around 10:00 PM, Zhu Qiyong, Huang Xiliang, and Zhu Kuiguang, employees of the Jing'an Temple Road National Product Commercial Field, were beaten by Dong Junchu, a Chinese police officer from the Lao Zha (Old Gate) Police Station No. 2966, and Kuolaike, an American police officer No. 325, with batons in front of the commercial field. Jiang Shiyi, Peng Qixiu, and Wang Shizong, three lawyers, filed a complaint with the French Concession Court. However, the court has no jurisdiction over the part of Kuolaike, who is of British nationality. Regarding the part of Dong Junchu's injury, Judge Wu Tingqi once gathered for questioning on June 6th, and instructed Dong to submit a summons to the shop guarantor to wait for rescheduling. It has been stated in this newspaper that if both parties have witnesses, they can submit written reports. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the rescheduling date had arrived. Judge Wu came to the second criminal court and first questioned the defendant Dong Junchu, saying, "During the previous court questioning, the plaintiffs Wang Xiliang and Zhu Kuiguang both pointed out in court that you were the one who hit them. What do you have to say?" Dong replied, "I did not hit them." The plaintiff Huang Xiliang was then questioned. According to his statement, he only recognized the numbers of the Chinese police officer who started the beating as 2966 and the western police officer as 325, but he did not see their faces clearly. Judge Wu asked why he only recognized the defendant's number. He replied that after he was beaten, he ran away, and the defendant did not give up and chased after him, so he recognized him. Asked if there were any other witnesses, he replied yes, there are Zhang Demei, Yu Pei, Zhang Hanchen, and other employees of the accounting department of the National Product Commercial Field, but none of them were present today. According to the plaintiff Zhu Kuiguang's statement, the numbers of the western police officer 325 and the Chinese police officer 2966 were seen during the beating. They first hit Zhu Qiyong, and then hit our heads and waists, and were injured. The waist was hit by the defendant, and the head was injured by the western police officer. According to the translator of the case of the western police officer 325, his name is Kuolaike, and he works at the Lao Zha Police Station. Judge Wu asked him, "At 10:00 PM on June 10th, how many people did the National Product Commercial Field officers arrest? Did you go with them?" The answer was, "I was also present, but only one person was arrested." Asked what his name was, he replied, "His surname is Song, he is not in court today." Asked, "Where was the defendant standing at this time?" The answer was, "On the road between Xizang Road and Nanjing Road, with the western police officer No. 194." Asked, "Did the three plaintiffs get injured, and did you start?" The answer was, "I don't know the situation." At this time, the defendant's agent Ding Rong stood up and requested that the western police chief Kanboer be allowed to report the case, because the western police chief saw the situation at the time and was the one who started. Judge Wu did not grant his request. The lawyer repeatedly requested, but it was not approved. He immediately began to debate. Lawyer Ding said that he would study this point further, or he would file an appeal. The plaintiffs' agents, lawyers Jiang and Peng, stood up successively and debated, asking the defendant to be punished for the crime of injury under Article 293 of the Criminal Law and Article 40 of the Criminal Law. Then, the defendant's agent, Lawyer Ding, continued to debate. Finally, the prosecutor expressed his opinion, saying that the facts of the case were very clear, and he asked for a judgment according to the law. The main text said, "Dong Junchu is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for the crime of harming people on the pretext of performing his duties. Before the judgment is finalized, the number of days of detention shall be deducted from the imprisonment at the rate of two days for one day. The part of Kuolaike will not be accepted. During the appeal period, Dong Junchu shall still be released on the original guarantee."

Car Falls into Creek 284

Li Dengshi, a local woman, 24 years old, a housewife of the Jue Lu Hotel on Xizang Road, lives at No. 65 Taoyuan Village, Lafayette Road, French Concession. At about 6:00 AM yesterday morning, she took her own car, the French Concession registration number is 667, and ordered the driver Tang Xiangsheng, (44 years old, Pudong native) to drive to Liuhe Town to offer incense. The second-hand driver Fang Guilin (40 years old, Anhui native) was also on the car. At about 6:30, when the car was no more than seven miles away from the destination, the place was remote and there were few pedestrians. Tang increased the speed and drove quickly. The road, although it was a coal cinder road, had been in disrepair for a long time, and was uneven. Suddenly, with a loud noise, the car fell into the creek on the side of the road, causing injuries to all three. Li's right foot was scraped, Fang Guilin was seriously injured, his right arm was fractured, and the back of his right hand was scraped. Tang Xiangsheng only suffered skin injuries, and his clothes were mostly drenched, like a chicken that fell into the water. Fortunately, the car was not damaged. Later, pedestrians arrived and helped to lift the car. Tang Xiangsheng drove back to Shanghai and sent the injured to the Baolong Hospital for treatment. Tang was diagnosed by a doctor and discharged from the hospital.

Ma Xiaoshi Dies After Jumping Off a Car 285

At 4:20 PM the day before yesterday, Ma Xiaoshi, a 32-year-old garbage collector from Haimen, was riding on a freight car No. 16693, traveling from east to west on Peikai'er Road. When the car was near Sheng Road, Ma urgently wanted to jump off, causing him to fall and be seriously injured. The driver, He Yiqing, heard about it and immediately stopped the car. After the Chinese police found out, they sent the car and the injured to the Tongren Hospital. The treatment was ineffective, and he soon died. The hospital notified the Huishan Police Station, ordering detectives to investigate. The body was carried to the Ferron Road autopsy station. Yesterday morning, the Shanghai Special District Court commissioned Prosecutor Guo Huaipu to examine the body and clarify the case. It was ruled that Ma Xiaoshi, who had died, had been careless and eager to jump off the freight car No. 16693, causing him to fall and die. The body was handed over to his younger brother, Ma Jiazhi, to sign for the coffin.

Wanyou Danfang (Universal Prescriptions) is Re-Published 292

Huang Tingsun, a famous doctor from eastern Zhejiang, selected and edited Wanyou Danfang, a guide to curing diseases. The collection period lasted for 30 years before it was completed. The first edition printed 10,000 copies, which were sold out in a short time. This time, it is being reprinted and published. The content is divided into four volumes, 26 subjects, four categories, 491 syndromes, and 971 prescriptions. The prescriptions listed are practical, and the medicines listed are sold on the market, making it easy for first aid. The entire book contains more than 60,000 words, over 170 pages, and a thick hardcover volume, selling at a special price of 6 jiao. At the beginning of the book, famous doctors in Shanghai, Xie Liheng, Tai Bowei, Fang Gongpu, Xu Banlong, Zhang Zanchen, and others, reviewed and inscribed it. The book is published by the Traditional Chinese Medicine Bookstore at No. 13 Shandong Road.
